Jamison Brereton

71
Agni
Par─Б┼Ыara ┼Ъ─Бktya
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh

The first of the Par─Б┼Ыara hymns in triс╣гс╣нubh, this is a curiously structured and very difficult hymn. It begins with a sexually suggestive verse describing the kindling of 194 I.71 the ritual fire by the fingers of the officiant manipulating the kindling sticks.

Verse 2 switches to the mythic past and a fairly standard and straightforward summary of the role of the Aс╣Еgirases in the opening of the Vala cave, but nothing in the hymn is straightforward after this. Verses treating the here-and-now of the ritual alternate with snippets of mythology.

The most dramatic mythological material is found discontinuously in verses 5 and 8, which treat the well-known if ill-understood story of the incest between Heaven and his daughter (see also X.61.5тАУ7, as well as Jamison 1991: 288тАУ301) and especially the punishment meted out to the offender by his avenger, who is clearly Agni. Since the birth of the Aс╣Еgirases resulted from this incest, this myth fits both the dedicand of the hymn and the Aс╣Еgiras verse (2) that follows the opening, and even the sexual innuendo of verse 1 may have evoked, or been evoked by, the incest theme.

The other mythological allusion is to M─Бtari┼ЫvanтАЩs stealing of fire (vs. 4); it is not clear whether this reference is meant to have any points of contact with the other mythological portions of the hymn. It does, however, connect with the theme of the interaction between gods and men, especially with Agni as go-between, found in verses 3, 4, and 7. Another puzzle is why Mitra and Varuс╣Зa intrude into this Agni hymn in verse 9, though the appearance of the Sun in that same verse takes us back to verse 2. Ritual concerns are the focus of vss. 3, 6, and 7.

In short, in terms of structure this hymn neither follows a point-to-point trajectory nor displays an omphalos/ring-compositional shape. Instead it seems to show, at least in its central sections, sets of interlocking, overlapping paired versesтАФ3 + 6, 4 + 7, 5 + 8тАФloosely nestled within a ring consisting of 2 + 9, and perhaps, more loosely still, 1 + 10.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe contiguous fingers, loving the affectionate Agni, as wives love their own husbands, plural ase him (with offered oblations), and honour him, who is entitled to honour, (with gesticulations), as the rays of light (are assiduous in the service) of the dawn, which is (at first) dark, (then) glimmering, and (finally) radiant.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The desirous females belonging to the same nest [=fingers] stimulate the desirous male [=Agni] close byтАФas wives of the same nest
[=household] stimulate their own husband.
The sisters [=fingers] have delighted in the dusky one and in the
ruddy one [=two fire-kindling sticks], like cows in the brilliantly
dawning dawn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The meter of this first verse almost serves as a transition from Par─Б┼ЫaraтАЩs Dvipad─Б Vir─Бj hymns that precede it to his Triс╣гс╣нubh ones beginning here (-I.73), as all four p─Бdas (as well as 2a) have openings of 5 (as if in Dvipad─Б Vir─Бj) and the first two are syntactic units. The hymn then settles down into a pattern of mostly 4- syllable openings.

The underlying fem. subject of this verse is universally taken to be the fingers of the priest producing fire by friction from the kindling sticks. The qualifier s├бn─лс╕╖─Бс╕е can be read with both the simile and the frame: the fingers belong to the same hand as the co-wives do to the same household. So Geldner, etc. The sexual innuendo fits the friction context well, in addition to setting the stage for the incest theme to come.

The object phrase ┼Ыy─Б╠Бviс╣Г ├бruс╣г─лm тАЬthe dusky and the ruddy [fem.]тАЭ is generally taken to refer to night and dawn (although Oldenberg [SBE and Noten] wishes to emend the text to fem. nom. pls. modifying the sisters, a generally bad idea). The identification with night and dawn is certainly supported by III.55.11, adduced by Geldner, etc., with the same vocabulary. However, it would essentially duplicate the simile of d (тАЬthey delighted in night and dawn, like cows in dawnтАЭ), a clumsiness that seems uncharacteristic of Par─Б┼Ыara, and one also wonders why the fingers would care about night and dawn. I think, instead, that this is another of Par─Б┼ЫaraтАЩs tricks, using color terms associated with the two time periods to pick out another referent entirely, namely the ar├бс╣Зi- (fem.) тАШkindling sticksтАЩ, which the fingers should care about, since they are manipulating them. The color differentiation is a little odd, but I don’t think it’s entirely out of the question. In X.184.3 the kindling sticks are called ‘golden’ (hiraс╣Зyay─л), and one can imagine that as the fire begins to catch hold, the upper stick might glow red, while the lower one would be wreathed in dark smoke.

Griffith

LOVING the loving One, as wives their husband, the sisters of one home have urged him forward,
Bright-coloured, even, as the cows love morning, dark, breaking forth to view, and redly beaming.

Oldenberg

The loving (women) have (amorously) excited 1 their lover, as wives of the same nest (house) their own husband. The sisters have delighted in the dark and in the red (goddess) 2, as the cows in the brightly shining dawn.

Ihn regten liebend an wie ihren Gatten, den liebenden, die Fraun im gleichen Sitze, Die Schwestern freun der schwarzen sich, der rothen, wie Rinder des in Glanz aufgehnden Morgens.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOur forefathers, the Aс╣Еgirasas, by their praises (of Agni), terrified the strong and daring devourer, (Paс╣Зi), by the sound; they made for us a path to the vast heaven, and obtained accessible day, the ensign of day, (─Аditya) and the cows (that had been stolen).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ketu = indicator or cause of day being known; ─Аditya, the sun

Jamison Brereton

Even the firm fastnesses did our fathers, the Aс╣Еgirases, break with their hymns, and the rock with their shout.
They made the way of lofty heaven for us; they found the day and the sun, the beacon of the ruddy dawn.

Griffith

Our sires with lauds burst e’en the firm-set fortress, yea, the Angirases, with roar, the mountain.
They made for us a way to reach high heaven, they found us day, light, day’s sign, beams of morning.

Oldenberg

Our fathers, the Aс╣Еgiras 1, have broken even the strong fortresses by their hymns, the rock by their shouting. They have opened to us the path of the great heaven; they have obtained day and sun and the shine of the dawn 2.

Geldner

Unsere V├дter, die Angiras┬┤ haben durch ihre Lieder selbst die starken Bollwerke, den Fels mit lautem Ruf erbrochen. Sie haben f├╝r uns den Gang des hohen Himmels hergestellt: sie haben den Tag, die Sonne, das Wahrzeichen der Morgenr├╢te gefunden.

Grassmann

Die festen Burgen brachen unsre V├дter durch Spruch den Fels die Angiras mit Krachen; Sie bahnten uns den Weg zum hohen Himmel, und fanden Tag und Sonne, Licht und Morgen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey secured hi, (Agni, in the sacrificial chamber), they made his worship the source of wealth; whence opulent votaries preserve his fires and practise his rites. Free from all (other) desire, assiduous in his adoration, and sustaining gods and men by their offerings, they come into his presence.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аryan = dhanasya sv─Бminaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

They set the truth in place and they set the vision of it in motion; just after that the voracious (visions) of the stranger are dispersed.
Never thirsting, (the [Aс╣ЕgirasesтАЩ/poetsтАЩ] visions), performing their tasks, go to the gods, strengthening their race with a pleasing offering.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A difficult verse with a discouragingly large number of competing interpretations. In outline, though not in detail, I follow GeldnerтАЩs interpretation: p─Бda a concerns the production of poetry and the poetic vision by our side, in contrast to the poetic visions of the stranger, our rival, in b. After the strangerтАЩs attempts are gotten rid of, the topic returns in cd to our poetic products, which have success. (Witzel Got┼Н basically follow Geldner, while Oldenberg [SBE] and Renou take b as coreferential with cd.) The first hemistich, esp. its first p─Бda, is highly alliterative and rhyming: d├бdhann с╣Ыt├бс╣Г dhan├бyann asya dh─лt├нm, ─Б╠Бd ├нd ary├│ didhiс╣гv├▓ v├нbhс╣Ыt─Бс╕е. The two parallel 3rd pl. verbs d├бdhan and dhan├бyan technically do not match in mood, since d├бdhan should be a subjunctive (the injunctive to this redupl. pres. should be either

*dadhat or dadhur, and the subjunctive of the latter verb should be dhan├бy─Бn; see Hoffmann 1967: 271 n. 13, who produces a tr. with subjunctive contrasting with preterite. However, in this context I think d├бdhan was created as a nonce injunctive to match the two an sequences in dhan├бyan. The subjects of these verbs are simultaneously the Aс╣Еgirases and the current poet-ritualists; the injunctive conveniently elides the difference between past and present action.

The beginning of b, ─Б╠Бd ├нd, generally has temporal value (тАЬjust after thatтАЭ) and is so tr. in the published translation But Par─Б┼Ыara uses the expression in causal value in I.67.8 and I.68.3, and a causal value is possible in the next verse (71.4); such an interpretation works better here, and I would therefore change the tr. to тАЬbecause of that тАжтАЭ The launching of their own poetic vision by our side scatters the visions of our opponents.

The sentiment, but not most of the vocabulary, echoes that in I.70.1, where the ar├н- is also the opponent.

The desid. adj. didhiс╣г├║- to тИЪdh─Б is based on the middle value of that root (тАШacquireтАЩ); so Heenen p. 165, though I do not subscribe to the additional semantic baggage Heenen attaches to the stem. It means тАШdesirous to acquireтАЩ, hence тАШgreedy, voraciousтАЩ. With most tr. I assume a pl. of dh─лt├н- as the referent.

Just as the injunctives of p─Бda a can have either presential or preterital value, the lack of verb in b allows the temporal value to be set by the preceding clause, hence applicable both to the current ritual situation and its mythological model. The published translation might be changed to тАЬare/were dispersed.тАЭ There is no agreement on what v├нbhс╣Ыtra- means here, but v├н тИЪbhс╣Ы generally means тАШdisperse, pull apart, carry awayтАЩ, and the form also needs to be considered in conjunction with v├нbhс╣Ыtaс╕е in the next vs. The тАЬunthirstingтАЭ dh─лt├н- belonging to us/the Aс╣Еgirases are implicitly contrasted with the voracious ones of the ar├н-, as Geldner, etc., point out.

With Grassmann, Oldenberg, Renou, I take ap├бsaс╕е as a nom. pl. fem.; Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) rather as a gen. sg. masc. referring to the singer/priest. This is certainly possible and would provide a neat contrast to the gen. sg. ary├бс╕е of b. I would prefer, however, to keep the possible reference to the Aс╣Еgirases alive. I would prefer not to take dev─Б╠Бn in d as a truncated gen. pl. construed with j├бnma (or as a second acc. with vardh├бyant─лс╕е тАЬstrengthening the gods, their raceтАЭ); therefore, despite the p─Бda boundary, I take it with ├бch─Б, which frequently governs dev─Б╠Бn (so, apparently, also Renou); cf. esp. I.132.5 (=139.1) dev─Бm╠Р├бch─Б n├б dh─лt├бyaс╕е, which is our underlying phrase.

Griffith

They stablished order, made his service fruitful; then parting them among the longing faithful,
Not thirsting after aught, they come, most active, while with sweet food the race of Gods they strengthen.

Oldenberg

They founded the Rita; they set into motion the thought of it 1. Thus then the widely-spread (prayers) 2 of the poor 3 which seek to obtain (wealth), which are free from thirst 4, the active, approach 5 the tribe of the gods 6, strengthening them by offering them delight.

Geldner

Sie stellten das Gesetz fest, sie brachten die Erkenntnis dieses in Umlauf. Seitdem sind die begehrlichen Gedanken des Nebenbuhlers wie Kinder, die noch getragen werden. Nur die gierlosen Gedanken des geschickten S├дngers gehen zu ihnen, indem sie das Geschlecht der G├╢tter mit Labsal st├дrken.

Grassmann

Sie schufen Opfer, regten sein Gebet an; und Lieder, buhlend, strebend, sich verbreitend, Sie nahn sich dann, nicht schmachtend, eifrig wirkend, mit Labung st├дrkend das Geschlecht der G├╢tter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the diffusive vital air excites Agni, he becomes bright and manifest in every mansion, and the instrumental tutor of the rite, imitating Bhс╣Ыgu, prevails on him to perform the function of messenger, as a prince who has become a friend sends an ambassador to his more powerful (conqueror).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

M─Бtari┼Ыvan = v─Бyu; here, it means, principal vital air, mukhyapr─Бс╣Зa; the legend about the dialogue amongst the five divided (vibhс╣Ыta) airs: ‘To them said the Ariс╣гс╣нa breaths: Be not astonished, for, I, having made myself five-fold, and having arrested the arrow, sustain (life)’;

Jenya = from jana, to be born; or, from ji, to conquer;

Legend: ’the gods and asuras were once engaged in combat; the former, being alarmed, entered into fire, therefore they call agni all the gods, who having made him their shield, overcame the asuras’ (Taittir─лya Samhit─Б 6.2.2.6-7); ’the gods having awoke agni and plural ced him before them at the morning sacrifice, repulsed, with him in their van, the asuras and r─Бkс╣гasas at the morning rite’ (Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 6.4)

Jamison Brereton

When M─Бtari┼Ыvan, borne away, stole him, and he of worthy birth came to be gleaming in every house, after that (the fire) of the Bhr╠еgus undertook the role of messenger, as if for a more powerful king, being associated with him.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another difficult verse, though it is clear that it alludes to the theft of fire by M─Бtari┼Ыvan in the first hemistich. This theft is expressed through word play: the verse begins m├бth─лt, which can mean either тАШchurn, rubтАЩ (to produce fire) or тАШstealтАЩ.

In this Agni context, esp. given vs. 1, which concerns the churning of fire, тАШchurnтАЩ would be the most likely reading - and so it is tr. by Geldner, Oldenberg (SBE), and Proferes (2007: 31). But the name M─Бtari┼Ыvan ends the p─Бda, and this mythological allusion would tip the balance towards тАШstealтАЩ (so Renou, Witzel Got┼Н).

The real problem comes in the middle of that p─Бda: the ppl. v├нbhс╣Ыtaс╕е. This form should mean тАШdispersedтАЩ or тАШcarried awayтАЩ, and grammatically it should modify m─Бtar├н┼Ыv─Б. However, sense would require it instead to qualify fire, the underlying direct object in the clause; fire is often carried away and dispersed in various locations. Cf. v├н тАж bharanta in the preceding hymn I.70.10 and discussion there, as well as the passages adduced by Oldenberg SBE, n. to vs. 4. There is no solution that satisfies both sense and syntax. Geldner suggests it’s a transferred epithet, from Agni to M─Бtari┼Ыvan; this seems a description of the problem, not a solution. Oldenberg suggests simply displacing it rightward to read it with the assumed subj. of p─Бda b, namely Agni (тАЬWhen M─Бtari┼Ыvan had produced him by attrition, he тАж, who was brought to many places, has come to every houseтАЭ), and Witzel Got┼Н apparently follow. But this kind of extraction from one clause and insertion in another is not syntactically possible in my opinion, esp. given that in its clause it is placed between the acc. referring to Agni (─лm) and the nom. m─Бtar├н┼Ыv─Б, so that its grammatical affiliation is emphasized. Narten reports a clever suggestion of HoffmannтАЩs, that the v├н- is really тАШbirdтАЩ, and the form means тАШcarried by a birdтАЩ (тАЬDas vedische Verbum math,тАЭ n. 38 [=KlSch p. 23 n. 38]), but M─Бtari┼Ыvan should no more be carried by a bird than be dispersed. In the end the least jarring rendering is RenouтАЩs тАЬsтАЩ├йtant transport├й ├з├а et l├а,тАЭ presumably referring to M─Бtari┼ЫvanтАЩs journey. My тАЬborne awayтАЭ reflects a similar notion, and I also toyed with the possibility that тАЬcarried awayтАЭ may have the same extended meaning as the English idiom, namely, тАЬovercome with excitement.тАЭ No doubt Par─Б┼Ыara recognized the trap he was setting, forcing the audience to find a way to interpret v├нbhс╣Ыtaс╕е with M─Бtari┼Ыvan rather than with the far more natural Agni.

As noted above, the subject of the next p─Бda must be Agni, established тАЬin every houseтАЭ (cf. V.11.4, X.91.2). Because of the accent on bh┼л╠Бt, the clause must be parallel to p─Бda a and is not the main clause, which is introduced by ─Б╠Бd ─лm in c.

On the second half of the verse see Proferes 2007: 30-31. AgniтАЩs role as messenger is of course well known: he travels between gods and men, heaven and earth. This regular route may be prefigured here by M─Бtari┼ЫvanтАЩs theft in a, for elsewhere it is clear that M. stole fire from heaven (e.g., I.93.6). It is also said that M.

bestowed the stolen fire on Bhс╣Ыgu (see nearby I.60.1), and so the epithet bhс╣Ы╠Бgav─Бna-, whatever its morphology, is apposite. What is unfamiliar is the simile, in which Agni serves as messenger as if for a more powerful king. According to Proferes, Agni is here тАЬdepicted тАж as the symbol of the presence of a leaderтАЩs authority within each household.тАЭ IтАЩm not sure, because AgniтАЩs d┼лt├б role involves traveling, not staying put. I am inclined to think the simile was generated simply from d┼лty├аm and is not meant to apply directly to Agni and his relationship to royal power.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen (the worshipper) offers an oblation to his great and illustrious protector, the grasping (r─Бkс╣гas), recognizing you, Agni, retires; but Agni, the archer, sends after him a blazing arrow from his dreadful bow, and the god bestows light upon his own daughter (the dawn).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Cf. Taittir─лya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 2.1.2.10)

Jamison Brereton

When he made the sap [=semen] for great Father Heaven, noting the caresses he stealthily crept up (on him).
The archer boldly loosed a missile at him (when) the god placed his тАЬsparkтАЭ in his own daughter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vivid account of the incestuous attack of Father Heaven on his own daughter (elsewhere Dawn) comes as a surprise in this hymn. The connection must be the fact that this incest led to the birth of the Aс╣Еgirases, who were the subject of vs. 2 (and possibly vs. 3); this birth is mentioned in the other incest verse, vs. 8cd, though without naming the Aс╣Еgirases. The other connection is that Agni, unnamed, is the avenger in this verse, shooting Heaven as he released his semen into his daughter. Although the avenger is usually identified as Rudra on the basis of postс╣Ъvic passages (see Geldner n. to vs. 5, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н), I have demonstrated (Hyenas, 288-97) that the original avenger was Agni. Note that ├бst─Б тАШarcherтАЩ is used of Agni in the last verse of the immediately preceding hymn (I.71.11). I also take Agni as the subj. of p─Бda b: like a hunter on his prey, he creeps up on the pair, having noticed the caresses (pс╣Ы┼Ыany├ас╕е) Heaven was bestowing on his daughter.

In addition I consider Agni to be the subject of p─Бda a (with most tr.), but the action there is harder to explain: how and why does Agni make the sap=semen for Heaven if he disapproves of HeavenтАЩs sexual designs on his daughter and in fact punishes him for the rape? For one thing, fire is unlikely to produce anything we might consider sap; in a naturalistic sense, making r├бsa for heaven would seem to be storing up rain. However, our notions of nature and Vedic IndiaтАЩs are often at odds.

That the same semen (or possibly its delivery agent, the penis) is called tv├нс╣гi- тАШspark, flareтАЩ in p─Бda d and, even more telling, is referred to as тАЬblazing semenтАЭ (┼Ы├║ci r├йtaс╕е) in 8b, brings it into fireтАЩs conceptual sphere. It may be that the flaring up of fire produces HeavenтАЩs semen. But what is AgniтАЩs motivation? IтАЩm afraid this remains mysterious; perhaps it was involuntary, produced by the flaring up just suggested.

Griffith

When man poured juice to Heaven, the mighty Father, he knew and freed himself from close embracement.
The archer boldly shot at him his arrow, and the God threw his splendour on his Daughter.

Oldenberg

When he had created sap to the great father Heaven, the knowing one stealthily approached the speckled (cows). The archer fiercely shot an arrow at him. The god turned his impetuous power against his daughter 1.

Geldner

Als er dem gro├Яen Vater Himmel Samen bereitet hatte, da schlich er heran, da er die Liebeslockungen bemerkt hatte. Der Sch├╝tze scho├Я dreist sein Gescho├Я auf ihn. Der Gott verrichtete seine Brunst an der eigenen Tochter.

Grassmann

Als Trank er bracht’ dem grossen Vater Himmel, entwand er klug sich aus der Tochter Armen, Der Sch├╝tze schoss den Pfeil auf ihn mit K├╝hnheit, da legt’ der Gott den Glanz in seine Tochter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen (the worshipper) kindles you in his own dwelling, and presents an oblation to you, daily desiring it, do you, Agni, augmented in two ways, (as middling and as best), increase his means of sustenance; may he whom you sen dwith his car to battle, return with wealth.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who will radiate widely for you here in his own house, or through the days will piously offer reverence belonging to (you) who are eager
for itтАФ
as the doubly lofty one, o Agni, you increase his vitality. He whom you speed will drive in the same chariot with Wealth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse returns us to the ritual here-and-now and is considerably easier to interpret than the scraps of mythology in the previous two verses. Still, there are a few puzzles.

The verb v├н bh─Бti тАШradiates widelyтАЩ is surprising, since its subject must be the mortal worshiper, even though Agni (or occasionally Dawn) is ordinarily the subject of this common verb. Oldenberg (SBE, repeated in Noten) suggests emending it to v├н dh─Бti тАШworshipsтАЩ (in OldenbergтАЩs tr.). (I sometimes get the feeling that in the Noten Oldenberg felt the need to stick with emendations heтАЩd suggested in his far more free-wheeling SBE tr., even though in his later years he was otherwise very reluctant to emend.) But a metaphorical sense of тАШradiateтАЩ works fine in the passage, as Geldner points out, citing parallels like VI.5.5, also of a mortal worshiper. And this would be an instance like v├нbhс╣Ыtaс╕е in 4 in which the most natural referent of a word is not the grammatically supported one. Oldenberg (SBE and Noten) also proposes to read dat. u┼Ыat├й in b, or rather suggests that the underlying form in sandhi was a dat. u┼Ыat├б, since the spellings u┼Ыat├│ ├бnu and u┼Ыat├й ├бnu тАЬbelong to the inventions of Vedic grammariansтАЭ (SBE n. 2 to vs. 6). This is certainly possible, but a gen. form u┼Ыat├│ would reflect what we might call the тАЬprolepticтАЭ use of the genitive for dative to express indirect object: the reverence was offered to you and so it is now yours. This colonization of the dative by the genitive is very common both in Vedic and in Classical Sanskrit, and already here it may reflect the weakening of the dative case that led to its disappearance in MIA. I certainly see no reason to take the transmitted u┼Ыat├│ as acc. pl. with dy┼л╠Бn, as Oldenberg (Noten) and Geldner (n. to 6b) tentatively suggest.

Griffith

Whoso, hath flames for thee within his dwelling, or brings the worship which thou lovest daily,
Do thou of double might increase his substance: may he whom thou incitest meet with riches.

Oldenberg

Augment, O Agni, twofold the strength of the man who worships 1 thee in his house, or offers adoration to the loving one 2 day by day. May he whom thou incitest be united with riches 3.

Geldner

Wer f├╝r dich im eigenen Haus von Begeisterung ergl├╝ht, oder dir Verehrung darbringt alle Tage dem Verlangenden, dessen Kraft mehre du doppelt, o Agni! Mit dem Reichtum soll im gleichen Wagen fahren, wen du aneiferst.

Grassmann

Wer, Agni, dir im eignen Hause Licht schafft, und t├дglich dir Anbetung zollt, dem holden, Dem mehre du die Kraft, als zwiefach starker, mit Reichthum geh im Bunde, wen du f├╢rderst.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAll (sacrificial) viands concentrate in Agni, as the seven great rivers flwo into the ocean; our food is not partaken of by our kinsmen, therefore do you, who know (all things), make our desires known to the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

All nourishments converge on Agni, like the seven youthful streams on the sea.
Our vitality is not widely perceptible in the form of our kin. Perceiving (it [=vitality]), find solicitude (for us) among the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The second hemistich consists of two contrasting halves: in c the speaker complains that his (тАЬourтАЭ) vitality (v├бyaс╕е), the same vitality that Agni was said to increase in 6c, is not to be seen throughout his kinsmen; this leaves Agni as the sole figure who will find solicitude (pr├бmati-) for him among the gods. Put thus, the passage does not make much sense in English. It relies on the close relationship between тАШsolicitudeтАЩ and kinship (see esp. I.31.9-10, I.108.1, X.23.7, also adduced by Geldner) in the RV. The word pr├бmati- denotes the kind of care and concern a father shows for his children (or sons) and is regularly associated with, and indeed identified with, the pit├бr- тАШfatherтАЩ (see, e.g., I.31.9, 10, 14, 16) and secondarily with the kin-group; cf. X.23.7 vidm─Б╠Бh├н te pr├бmatiс╣Г deva j─Бmiv├бt тАЬfor we know your (fatherly) solicitude, o god, like that of kin.тАЭ Since in our passage the j─Бm├н- has proved disappointing, the poet turns to Agni for satisfaction. The question then is what is the relationship between vitality and solicitude, which seem conceptually distant. This is less clear, but the connection is also found in the pr├бmati-heavy I.31 already cited; cf. I.31.10ab tv├бm agne pr├бmatis tv├бm pit─Б╠Бsi nas, tv├бс╣Г vayaskс╣Ы╠Бt t├бva j─Бm├бyo vay├бm тАЬYou, Agni, are (fatherly) solicitude, you a father to us. You are creator of vitality; we are your kin.тАЭ In the immediately preceding verse (I.31.9) Agni is also called tan┼лkс╣Ы╠Бt- тАШbody-creatorтАЩ. The balanced pairing of tan┼лkс╣Ы╠Бt- and vayaskс╣Ы╠Бt- in a paternal context suggests that in producing children the father creates both the physical body and the intangible essence of life that together make up a living being - тАШlife-forceтАЩ might be a reasonable rendering of v├бyas - and the fatherтАЩs pr├бmati- seems to be the catalyst that brings them together. Moreover, at least on the evidence of our passage, v├бyas- seems to be something that can be shared by the kingroup, but in this case is not, and in such circumstances if one cannot rely on the shared vitality of his relatives, he must look only to his father and his fatherтАЩs solicitude. For another association of vitality and the father in Par─Б┼ЫaraтАЩs work, see I.73.1.

The published translation does not convey this very well. In c I would replace тАЬis not widely perceptibleтАЭ with тАЬis not widely evidentтАЭ or тАЬdoes not appear throughout.тАЭ I also question my supplying an object (vitality) with cikitv─Б╠Бn; I now think this simply characterizes Agni as the perceptive one or indicates that he perceives the situation as a whole. The same word cikitv─Б╠Бn does seem to take an object in 5b, however. Against the Pp. I prefer to take vid─Б╠Бas a lengthened 2nd sg. imperative rather than subj. vid─Б╠Бs, though there are no real implications either way.

Griffith

All sacrificial viands wait on Agni as the Seven mighty Rivers seek the ocean.
Not by our brethren was our food discovered: find with the Gods care for us, thou who knowest.

Oldenberg

Every nourishment goes towards Agni 1, as the seven young 2 rivers (flow) into the ocean. Our strength does not shine from kinsmen 3. Do thou therefore who knowest this, procure among the gods kindness for us.

Geldner

Zu Agni gesellen sich alle Kr├дfte wie die sieben j├╝ngsten Str├╢me zum Meere. Unsere St├дrke ist nicht durch Verwandte ansehnlich. M├╢gest du als Kundiger bei den G├╢ttern Vorliebe finden.

Grassmann

Zu ihm, dem Agni, streben alle Speisen, wie zu dem Meer die sieben schnellen Str├╢me; Nicht bei Verwandten ward uns Nahrung sichtbar; F├╝rsorge schaffe kundig uns bei G├╢ttern.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдзрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдореН (VC)
  • рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ
  • рдкрд░рд╛рд╢рд░рдГ рд╢рд╛рдХреНрддрдГ
  • рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН
  • рдзреИрд╡рддрдГ
рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд╣ рдХреИрд╕рд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЛ (рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХрд╛ рд╣реЗрддреБ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд╛ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рдкреНрд░рдорддрд┐рдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддрд╛ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рдЬреАрд╡рди рдХрд╛ (рд╡рд┐рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреЗ) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХрд░рд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕ (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╕рдм (рдкреГрдХреНрд╖рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдореНрдкрд░реНрдХ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛ рджреАрдкреНрддрд┐ (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдореН) рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рд╡рд╛ (рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддрдГ) рдирджреА рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╢рд░реАрд░ рдХреЛ рдЧрдорди рдХрд░рд╛рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рд╕рдкреНрдд) рд╕рд╛рдд рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдг, рдЕрдкрд╛рди, рд╡реНрдпрд╛рди, рдЙрджрд╛рди, рд╕рдорд╛рди рдЗрди рдкрд╛рдБрдЪ рдХреЗ рдФрд░ рд╕реВреНрддреНрд░рд░реВрдк рдЖрддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрдордХрд╛рд░рдгрд╕реНрде рддрдерд╛ (рдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрдГ) рд░реБрдзрд┐рд░ рд╡рд╛ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреА рдЧрддрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ (рди) рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдЕрднрд┐рд╕рдЪрдиреНрддреЗ) рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ рдореВрд░реНрдЦ рд╡рд╛ рджреБрдГрдЦ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА (рдЬрд╛рдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рди) рдирд╣реАрдВ рдмрд╕реЗрдВ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИрдВред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░ рдХреЛ рдирджреА рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдЖрджрд┐ рдЧрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░рддреА рд╣реИрдВ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╕рдм рдкреБрддреНрд░ рд╡рд╛ рдХрдиреНрдпрд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреНрдп рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛ рд╡реНрд░рддреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рдХреЗ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╣ рд╕реЗ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░ рдЙрдирдХреЛ рдЗрд╕реА рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рд╕рджрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗрдВред рдкреБрддреНрд░реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдХреА рдЙрддреНрддрдо рд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдХреЛрдИ рдмреЬрд╛ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдирд╣реАрдВ рд╣реИ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдпрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдкреНрд░рдорддрд┐рдВ рд╡рд┐рджрд╛ рд╡рдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреЗ рддрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреГрдХреНрд╖рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрдпреЛ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддрдГ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдиреН рдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрд░реНрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рднрд┐рд╕рдЪрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрддреЛ рд╡рдпрдВ рдореВрд░реНрдЦрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрджреБрдГрдЦрджрд╛рднрд┐рд░реНрдЬрд╛рдорд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╣ рди рд╕рдВрд╡рд╕реЗрдо рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд╕реНрд╕ рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН) рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрддрдореН (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдЕрдЦрд┐рд▓рд╛рдГ (рдЕрднрд┐) рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ (рдкреГрдХреНрд╖рдГ) рдпрд╛рдГ рдкреГрдЪрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕рдореНрдкрд░реНрдХрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реНрдпрдГ (рд╕рдЪрдиреНрддреЗ) рд╕рдорд╡рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ (рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдореН) рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╡рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╕реНрд░рд╡рддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдиреН (рд╕рдкреНрдд) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдкрд╛рдирд╡реНрдпрд╛рдиреЛрджрд╛рдирд╕рдорд╛рдирд╕реВрддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрдордХрд╛рд░рдгрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреН (рдпрд╣реНрд╡реАрдГ) рдорд╣рддреНрдпреЛ рд░реБрдзрд┐рд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рджрд┐рдЧрддрдпрдГ (рди) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдЬрд╛рдорд┐рднрд┐рдГ) рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрднрд┐рдГ (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗ (рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреЗ) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ (рд╡рдпрдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдп (рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрдЧреБрдгреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд╛ (рдкреНрд░рдорддрд┐рдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдореН (рдЪрд┐рдХрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН) рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдкрдХреЛ рд╡рд╛ рее рен рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░рдВ рдирджреНрдпрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рджрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдВрдпреБрдЮреНрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдереИрд╡ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╛ рдХрдиреНрдпрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпреНрдпреЗрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡реНрд░рддреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдп рдпреБрд╡рд╛рд╜рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╡рд╛рд╣рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╕рдиреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдиреБрддреНрдкрд╛рджреНрдп рддреЗрднреНрдпрд╕реНрддрдереИрд╡ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╣рдпреЗрдпреБрд░рдиреЗрди рд╕рдордГ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рджрдзрд┐рдХ рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░реЛ рди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рее рен рее

рд╕реЛ рд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рджреНрдпреМрд░реН рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ ред рджрд┐рд╡реЗрдГ рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред рдЕрднреАрдХреЗ рдЖрд╕рдиреНрдиреЗ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдЪрд┐рд░рд╛рджреЗрд╡ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдг-рдЧреБрдг-рд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЬрдирдпрддреН рдЬрдирдпрддреБ ред рдЬрдиреЗрд░реНрд▓реЗрдЯреН ред рд╢рд░реНрдзрдВ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдЕрдирд╡рджреНрдпрдорд╡рджреНрдпрд░рд╣рд┐рддрдореН ред ‘рдирдЮреНрд╕реБрднреНрдпрд╛рдореН’ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрд╛рдиреНрддреЛрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рддрд░реБрдгрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзрд┐рдпрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХрд░реНрдордирд┐рд░рддрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордирд┐рд╖реНрдардВ рд╡рд╛ ред рдИрджреГрд╢рдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН, рд╕реВрджрдпрдЪреН рдЪ рд╕реВрджрдпрддреБ рдЪ ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдкрд╛рдкрдореН ред рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рд▓реНрд▓реЗрдЯреН, рддрд┐рдЩрдГ рдкрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛рдиреНрди рдирд┐рд╣рдиреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдИрджреГрд╢реЛ рд╣рд┐ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕реНрддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐ ред ‘рд╕ рдПрд╡рд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрддреЗрдЬреЛ рджрдзрд╛рддрд┐ рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реНрдпреЗрд╡ рднрд╡рддрд┐’ `рдЗрддрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН ред

рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рджрд╛рд╣реБрдГ - рдпрджрд┐рддрд┐ рд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпрдГ, рдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдВ рд╢рд░реНрдзрдордирд╡рджреНрдпрдВ рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдирдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзрд┐рдпрдВ рдиреГрдкрддрд┐рдВ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯрдореБрджрдХрдорд╛рдирдЯреН рд╕реЛрдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдореЗрд╡ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рддреЗрдЬреЛ рдЬрдирдпрддреБ рддреЗрдЬреЛрд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрд┐ рдЪ рд╕реВрджрдпрддреБ рдЗрддрд┐ ред ‘рдЪрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ рдЪ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рддрд┐рдЩреЛ рдирд┐рдШрд╛рддрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ, рддрд┐рдЩрдГ рдкрд░рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that (digestive) faculty (of Agni) with regards food, be imparted to the devout and illustrious protector of priests, as the source of virile vigour; and may Agni be born as (his) robust, irreproachable, youthful and intelligent son, and instrumental gate him (to acts of worship).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Retas = water; hence, ‘may fire and water, or heat and moister, be spread through the earth for the genitive ration of corn’ is an alternative rendering

Jamison Brereton

When the (missileтАЩs) sharp point reached the lord of men [=Agni] (for him) to release it, Heaven, at the moment of contact, (released) the blazing semen poured out.
Agni engendered the faultless young troop of good intention [=Aс╣Еgirases] and sweetened it.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The incest myth treated in vs. 5 returns here with no more clarity. The various alternative treatments are too numerous to discuss here, so I will present only my own version, some of whose details I have adopted from others.

The first hemistich describes again Agni as the avenger, loosing his weapon at Heaven in the midst of the latterтАЩs sexual encounter with his daughter. In p─Бda a the t├йjaс╕е, the sharp point of the arrow, reaches the lord of men (=Agni, in my view), so that he can shoot it. I do not understand why his preparation for shooting should be described thus, and in a phrase ─Б╠Бnaс╣н + ACC we might expect the acc. to express the target of the arrow.

Nonetheless, Heaven is not otherwise called nс╣Ыp├бti-, and it would be odd to give him this positive epithet in this situation. For Agni as an archer whose arrow has a t├йjassee VI.3.5 s├б ├нd ├бsteva pr├бti dh─Бd asiс╣гy├б├▒, ch├н┼Ы─лta t├йj├▓ ‘yas─Б n├б dh─Б╠Бr─Бm тАЬHe, just like an archer, has aimed (his arrow), about to shoot. He has whetted its point like a blade of copper.тАЭ I take iс╣г├й in this p─Бda as an infinitive to тИЪiс╣г тАШimpel, sendтАЩ (others interpret it as тАШto enjoyтАЩ); I then supply a form of this same verb in the next p─Бda, which otherwise lacks one.

Note that the product of this incest, the young troop (┼Ы├бrdham тАж y├║v─Бnam), is characterized as both тАШfaultlessтАЩ (anavady├бm) and тАШwell-intentionedтАЩ (sv─Бdhy├аm), asserting their goodness despite the circumstances of their birth.

Griffith

When light hath filled the Lord of men for increase, straight from the heaven descends the limpid moisture.
Agni hath brought to light and filled with spirit the youthful host blameless and well providing.

Oldenberg

1 When the sharp splendour 2 reached the lord of men to incite him 3, the bright sperm poured down from Heaven (or, from the god Dyaus)4, Agni produced 5 and furthered the blameless, young, well-wishing host 6.

Keith

What time his glory urged the lord to strength,
Then (did) Dyaus (let) the pure seed be sprinkled openly;
Agni begot the host, the blameless, the youthful,
The worshipping, and gave it impulse.

Wenn ihn, den Herrn, zur Labung Glanz erf├╝llt hat, dann str├╢mt vom Himmel nieder reiner Same; Die tadellose junge Schar hat Agni, die sorgende, erzeugt und gross gezogen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe sun, who traverses alone the path of heaven with the speed of thought, is at once lord of all treasures; the two kings, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, with bounteous hands, are the guardians of the precious ambrosia of our cattle.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who, like thought, travels his roads in a single day, the Sun alone is entirely master of goods,
(as are) the kings Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, they of good hands, who guard their own dear immortal thing [=milk?] within the cows.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As mentioned in the published introduction, the reason for including this verse, containing the Sun and Mitra and Varuс╣Зa but no mention of Agni, isnтАЩt clear.

However, it may be that Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, the guardians of the moral and ethical order, and their all-seeing eye, the Sun, who observes all behavior, are brought in as witnesses of the shocking incest of the last verse and the appropriate punishment inflicted by Agni.

Griffith

He who like thought goes swiftly on his journey, the Sun, alone is ever Lord of riches.
The Kings with fair hands, Varuna and Mitra, protect the precious nectar in our cattle.

Oldenberg

He who traverses the paths quickly 1 like thought, the Sun alone rules over wealth altogether. (There are) the two kings Mitra and Varuna with graceful hands 2, who watch over the beloved ambrosia 3 in the cows.

Geldner

Der Sonnengott, der wie der Gedanke in k├╝rzester Frist seine Wege geht, gebeut allein ├╝ber das Gut insgesamt, w├дhrend die K├╢nige Mitra und Varuna, die sch├╢nh├дndigen, die liebe G├╢tterspeise in den K├╝hen bewachen.

Grassmann

Die Sonn’ allein, die wie der Geist die Wege im Nu durcheilt, besitzet allen Reichthum; Die Herrscher Mitra, Varuna, die milden, den lieben Nektar in den K├╝hen hegend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDissolve not, Agni, our ancestral friendship, for you are cognizant of the past as well as of the present; in like manner as light (speeds over) the sky, so decay impairs (my body); think of me before that source of destruction (prevails).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Amс╣Ыtatvam prayacchati y─Бvat, asking Agni, therefore, to grant immortality

Jamison Brereton

Agni, do not neglect our ancestral partnerships, being preeminent as a wise poet.
Old age alters our form like a cloud. Be attentive (to us) in the face of this curse.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another apparent non sequitur. I have nothing to say about the morphology of the famous crux vid├║с╕е, which occurs also in VII.18.2 in the same phrase with the same irregular sandhi (abh├н vid├║с╣г kav├нс╕е s├бn). I do consider it a nom. sg., not acc. pl.

For further disc. see comm. at VII.18.2.

Griffith

O Agni, break not our ancestral friendship, Sage as thou art, endowed with deepest knowledge.
Old age, like gathering cloud, impairs the body: before that evil be come nigh protect me.

Oldenberg

Do not forget, O Agni, who art a sage possessed of knowledge 1, our paternal friendship. Old age impairs the appearance (of men) as a cloud (covers the sun or the sky). Before this curse (attains us), think thou (of us) 2.

Geldner

Vergi├Я nicht, Agni, unsere v├дterliche Freundschaft, der du als Seher die Wissenden ├╝bertriffst! Das Alter ver├дndert das Aussehen wie die Wolke ihr Aussehen ├дndert. Bevor solcher Vorwurf erhoben wird, gedenke unser!

Grassmann

O Agni, der du bist ein weiser Seher, vergiss nicht unsre v├дterliche Freundschaft; Das Alter mindert Sch├╢nheit wie der Nebel, vor solchem Uebel wollest du uns wahren.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд╣ рдХреИрд╕рд╛ рд╣реЛ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╕рдм рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдП рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН ! рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИрдВред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд░реВрдкрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдо рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдореЗрдВ рдирд╣реАрдВ рджреАрдЦрддреЗ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдкрди рдЖрджрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдирд╖реНрдЯ рди рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ, рдХрд┐рдиреНрддреБ рд╣рдо рд╕рдм рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдз рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдЫреЛреЬрдХрд░ рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рд╣реЛрдХреЗ рд╕рдм рдХрд╛рд▓ рдореЗрдВ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд░рд╣реЗрдВ рее резреж рее рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░, рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖, рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА, рдкреБрд░реБрд╖, рдмрд┐рдЬреБрд▓реА рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреА рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐ рд╕рдордЭрдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ ! рдкрд╛рд╡рдХрд╡рдЬреНрдЬрд░рд┐рдорд╛ рдХрд╡рд┐рд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреБрдГ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдирдореЛ рд░реВрдкрдВ рди рддрдерд╛ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдкреБрд░рд╛ рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╕рдЦреНрдпрд╛ рдорд╛рднрд┐рдкреНрд░рдорд░реНрд╖рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддреЗрд░реНрдирд╛рд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдзреАрд╣рд┐ рдПрд╡рдВ рднреВрддрдГ рд╕рдиреН рдпрдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдорд┐рдирд╛рддрд┐ рддрдВ рджреВрд░реАрдХрд░реБ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирдГ рд╕ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХреАрджреГрд╢ рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдорд╛) рдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзреЗ (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╜рднрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдд рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рдиреН (рд╕рдЦреНрдпрд╛) рдорд┐рддреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ (рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐) рдкрд┐рддреГрднреНрдп рдЖрдЧрддрд╛рдирд┐ (рдкреНрд░) рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рдорд░реНрд╖рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдпреЗрдГ (рдЕрднрд┐) рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ (рд╡рд┐рджреБрдГ) рд╡реЗрддреНрддрд╛ (рдХрд╡рд┐рдГ) рдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдГ (рд╕рдиреН) рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ (рдирднрдГ) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд░реВрдкрдореН) рд░реВрдкрд╡рджреНрд╡рд╕реНрддреБ (рдЬрд░рд┐рдорд╛) рдПрддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреЗрд░реНрднрд╛рд╡рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ (рдорд┐рдирд╛рддрд┐) рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдкреБрд░рд╛) рдкреБрд░рд╛рддрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рддрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдЙрдХреНрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ (рдЕрднрд┐рд╢рд╕реНрддреЗрдГ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ (рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЙрдкрд░рд┐рднрд╛рд╡реЗ (рдЗрд╣рд┐) рд╕реНрдорд░ рее резреж рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рдпрдерд╛ рд░реВрдкрд╡рдиреНрддрдГ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдГ рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдорд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗрд╜рджреГрд╢реНрдпрд╛ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ред рддрдерд╛рд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рдЦрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рдирд┐ рдирд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдирд┐ рди рднрд╡реЗрдпреБрд░реНрдпрддрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдзрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд╛рдп рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░рдВ рд╕реБрд╣реГрджреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд┐рдирдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо рее резреж рее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╕рднрд╛рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпреБрджреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирдВ рдХреГрддрдордд рдПрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рд╡ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рдЬрд╕реЗ рдЖрдХрд╛рд░рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрде рд╕реВрдХреНрд╖реНрдо рдЕрд╡рд╕реНрдереЗрдд рдЕрдВрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдд рджрд┐рд╕рдд рдирд╛рд╣реАрдд рддрд╕реЗ рдЖрдордЪреА рдореИрддреНрд░реА рд╡рдЧреИрд░реЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдирд╖реНрдЯ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛ рдирдпреЗрдд рддрд░ рдЖрдореНрд╣реА рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡реА рд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдз рд╕реЛрдбреВрди рдкрд░рд╕реНрдкрд░ рдорд┐рддреНрд░ рдмрдиреВрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдХрд╛рд│реА рд╕реБрдЦреА рд░рд╛рд╣рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резреж рее
